<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>
<s> they had offered her sportive bets and exchanged with her all sorts of free talk and knowing innuendoes <\s>
<s> they pointed out to her who was on the course and the who was not always the person a young lady should know <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>
<s> how easily she takes it <\s>
<s> one man whispered to another <\s>
<s> the begum's made of money the friend replied <\s>
<s> how easily she takes what <\s>
<s> has anybody lost any money <\s>
<s> lady clavering said she was happy in the morning because sir francis had promised her not to bet <\s>
<s> welbore the country neighbour of the claverings was passing the carriage when he was called back by the begum who rallied him for wishing to cut her <\s>
<s> why didn't he come before <\s>
<s> why didn't he come to lunch <\s>
<s> her ladyship was in great delight she told him she told everybody that she had won five pounds in a lottery <\s>

<s> welbore looked so particularly knowing and withal melancholy that a dismal apprehension seized upon major pendennis <\s>
<s> he would go and look after the horses and those rascals of postillions who were so long in coming round <\s>

<s> the good natured begum asked <\s>
<s> the major pretended a headache from the fatigue and sunshine of the day <\s>
<s> the carriage wheeled off the course and took its way londonwards not the least brilliant equipage in that vast and picturesque procession <\s>
<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>
<s> after a slumber of about an hour and a half the heir of the house began to exhibit symptoms of wakefulness stretching his youthful arms over the major's face and kicking his sister's knees as she sate opposite to him <\s>
<s> when the amiable youth was quite restored to consciousness he began a sprightly conversation <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>

<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>
<s> they had offered her sportive bets and exchanged with her all sorts of free talk and knowing innuendoes <\s>
<s> they pointed out to her who was on the course and the who was not always the person a young lady should know <\s>

<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>
<s> after a slumber of about an hour and a half the heir of the house began to exhibit symptoms of wakefulness stretching his youthful arms over the major's face and kicking his sister's knees as she sate opposite to him <\s>
<s> when the amiable youth was quite restored to consciousness he began a sprightly conversation <\s>
<s> i say ma he said i've gone and done it this time i have <\s>
<s> what have you gone and done franky dear <\s>
<s> how much is seventeen half crowns <\s>
<s> two pound and half a crown ain't it <\s>
<s> i drew borax in our lottery but i bought podasokus and man milliner of leggat minor for two open tarts and a bottle of ginger beer <\s>
<s> you little wicked gambling creature how dare you begin so soon <\s>
<s> hold your tongue if you please <\s>
<s> who ever asked your leave miss <\s>

<s> you'll tip me all the same you know when i go back and here he broke out into a laugh <\s>
<s> i say ma shall i tell you something <\s>
<s> the begum expressed her desire to hear this something and her son and heir continued when me and strong was down at the grand stand after the race and i was talking to leggat minor who was there with his governor i saw pa look as savage as a bear <\s>
<s> and i say ma leggat minor told me that he heard his governor say that pa had lost seven thousand backing the favourite <\s>
<s> 2002 he went to pay his respects to the carriage to which and to the side of her mamma the dove coloured author of mes larmes had by this time returned <\s>
<s> indefatigable old major pendennis was in waiting upon lady clavering and had occupied the back seat in her carriage the box being in possession of young hopeful under the care of captain strong <\s>
<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>
<s> they had offered her sportive bets and exchanged with her all sorts of free talk and knowing innuendoes <\s>
<s> they pointed out to her who was on the course and the who was not always the person a young lady should know <\s>
<s> when pen came up to lady clavering's carriage he had to push his way through a crowd of these young bucks who were paying their court to miss amory in order to arrive as near that young lady who beckoned him by many pretty signals to her side <\s>
<s> je lay vue she said elle a de bien beaux yeux vous etes un monster <\s>
<s> said pen with a laugh hone suit qui mal y peens <\s>
<s> my young friend yonder is as well protected as any young lady in christendom <\s>
<s> she has her mamma on one side her pretend on the other <\s>
<s> could any harm happen to a girl between those two <\s>
<s> one does not know what may or may not arrive said miss blanche in french when a girl has the mind and when she is pursued by a wicked monster like you <\s>
<s> figure to yourself major that i come to find monsieur your nephew near to a cab by two ladies and a man oh such a man <\s>
<s> and who ate lobsters and who laughed who laughed <\s>
<s> it did not strike me that the man laughed pen said and as for lobsters i thought he would have liked to eat me after the lobsters <\s>
<s> he shook hands with me and gripped me so that he bruised my glove black and blue <\s>
<s> he is a young surgeon <\s>
<s> he comes from clavering <\s>
<s> don't you remember the gilt pestle and mortar in high street <\s>
<s> if he attends you when you are sick continued miss amory he will kill you <\s>
<s> he will serve you right for you are a monster <\s>

<s> i hope so said his friend and they disappeared to enjoy themselves among the sticks <\s>
<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>

<s> has anybody lost any money <\s>

<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>

<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>

<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>

<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>

<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>

<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>

<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>

<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>
<s> they had offered her sportive bets and exchanged with her all sorts of free talk and knowing innuendoes <\s>
<s> they pointed out to her who was on the course and the who was not always the person a young lady should know <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>
<s> how easily she takes it <\s>
<s> one man whispered to another <\s>
<s> the begum's made of money the friend replied <\s>
<s> how easily she takes what <\s>
<s> has anybody lost any money <\s>
<s> lady clavering said she was happy in the morning because sir francis had promised her not to bet <\s>
<s> welbore the country neighbour of the claverings was passing the carriage when he was called back by the begum who rallied him for wishing to cut her <\s>
<s> why didn't he come before <\s>
<s> why didn't he come to lunch <\s>
<s> her ladyship was in great delight she told him she told everybody that she had won five pounds in a lottery <\s>

<s> welbore looked so particularly knowing and withal melancholy that a dismal apprehension seized upon major pendennis <\s>
<s> he would go and look after the horses and those rascals of postillions who were so long in coming round <\s>

<s> the good natured begum asked <\s>
<s> the major pretended a headache from the fatigue and sunshine of the day <\s>
<s> the carriage wheeled off the course and took its way londonwards not the least brilliant equipage in that vast and picturesque procession <\s>
<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>
<s> after a slumber of about an hour and a half the heir of the house began to exhibit symptoms of wakefulness stretching his youthful arms over the major's face and kicking his sister's knees as she sate opposite to him <\s>
<s> when the amiable youth was quite restored to consciousness he began a sprightly conversation <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>

<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>
<s> they had offered her sportive bets and exchanged with her all sorts of free talk and knowing innuendoes <\s>
<s> they pointed out to her who was on the course and the who was not always the person a young lady should know <\s>

<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>
<s> after a slumber of about an hour and a half the heir of the house began to exhibit symptoms of wakefulness stretching his youthful arms over the major's face and kicking his sister's knees as she sate opposite to him <\s>
<s> when the amiable youth was quite restored to consciousness he began a sprightly conversation <\s>
<s> i say ma he said i've gone and done it this time i have <\s>
<s> what have you gone and done franky dear <\s>
<s> how much is seventeen half crowns <\s>
<s> two pound and half a crown ain't it <\s>
<s> i drew borax in our lottery but i bought podasokus and man milliner of leggat minor for two open tarts and a bottle of ginger beer <\s>
<s> you little wicked gambling creature how dare you begin so soon <\s>
<s> hold your tongue if you please <\s>
<s> who ever asked your leave miss <\s>

<s> you'll tip me all the same you know when i go back and here he broke out into a laugh <\s>
<s> i say ma shall i tell you something <\s>
<s> the begum expressed her desire to hear this something and her son and heir continued when me and strong was down at the grand stand after the race and i was talking to leggat minor who was there with his governor i saw pa look as savage as a bear <\s>
<s> and i say ma leggat minor told me that he heard his governor say that pa had lost seven thousand backing the favourite <\s>
<s> 2002 he went to pay his respects to the carriage to which and to the side of her mamma the dove coloured author of mes larmes had by this time returned <\s>
<s> indefatigable old major pendennis was in waiting upon lady clavering and had occupied the back seat in her carriage the box being in possession of young hopeful under the care of captain strong <\s>
<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>
<s> they had offered her sportive bets and exchanged with her all sorts of free talk and knowing innuendoes <\s>
<s> they pointed out to her who was on the course and the who was not always the person a young lady should know <\s>
<s> when pen came up to lady clavering's carriage he had to push his way through a crowd of these young bucks who were paying their court to miss amory in order to arrive as near that young lady who beckoned him by many pretty signals to her side <\s>
<s> je lay vue she said elle a de bien beaux yeux vous etes un monster <\s>
<s> said pen with a laugh hone suit qui mal y peens <\s>
<s> my young friend yonder is as well protected as any young lady in christendom <\s>
<s> she has her mamma on one side her pretend on the other <\s>
<s> could any harm happen to a girl between those two <\s>
<s> one does not know what may or may not arrive said miss blanche in french when a girl has the mind and when she is pursued by a wicked monster like you <\s>
<s> figure to yourself major that i come to find monsieur your nephew near to a cab by two ladies and a man oh such a man <\s>
<s> and who ate lobsters and who laughed who laughed <\s>
<s> it did not strike me that the man laughed pen said and as for lobsters i thought he would have liked to eat me after the lobsters <\s>
<s> he shook hands with me and gripped me so that he bruised my glove black and blue <\s>
<s> he is a young surgeon <\s>
<s> he comes from clavering <\s>
<s> don't you remember the gilt pestle and mortar in high street <\s>
<s> if he attends you when you are sick continued miss amory he will kill you <\s>
<s> he will serve you right for you are a monster <\s>

<s> i hope so said his friend and they disappeared to enjoy themselves among the sticks <\s>
<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>

<s> has anybody lost any money <\s>

<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>

<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>

<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>

<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>

<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>

<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>

<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>

<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>

<s> a number of dandies and men of a certain fashion of military bucks of young rakes of the public offices of those who may be styled men's men rather than ladies' had come about the carriage during its station on the hill and had exchanged a word or two with lady clavering and a little talk a little chaff some of the most elegant of the men styled their conversation with miss amory <\s>
<s> they had offered her sportive bets and exchanged with her all sorts of free talk and knowing innuendoes <\s>
<s> they pointed out to her who was on the course and the who was not always the person a young lady should know <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>
<s> how easily she takes it <\s>
<s> one man whispered to another <\s>
<s> the begum's made of money the friend replied <\s>
<s> how easily she takes what <\s>
<s> has anybody lost any money <\s>
<s> lady clavering said she was happy in the morning because sir francis had promised her not to bet <\s>
<s> welbore the country neighbour of the claverings was passing the carriage when he was called back by the begum who rallied him for wishing to cut her <\s>
<s> why didn't he come before <\s>
<s> why didn't he come to lunch <\s>
<s> her ladyship was in great delight she told him she told everybody that she had won five pounds in a lottery <\s>

<s> welbore looked so particularly knowing and withal melancholy that a dismal apprehension seized upon major pendennis <\s>
<s> he would go and look after the horses and those rascals of postillions who were so long in coming round <\s>

<s> the good natured begum asked <\s>
<s> the major pretended a headache from the fatigue and sunshine of the day <\s>
<s> the carriage wheeled off the course and took its way londonwards not the least brilliant equipage in that vast and picturesque procession <\s>
<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>
<s> don't you think we could get up races at clavering mamma <\s>
<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>
<s> it's a national amusement you know and we could have a clavering ball and we might have dances for the tenantry and rustic sports in the park oh it would be charming <\s>
<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
<s> the turf is a very expensive amusement my dear lady major pendennis answered with such a rueful face that the begum rallied him and asked laughingly whether he had lost money on the race <\s>
<s> after a slumber of about an hour and a half the heir of the house began to exhibit symptoms of wakefulness stretching his youthful arms over the major's face and kicking his sister's knees as she sate opposite to him <\s>
<s> when the amiable youth was quite restored to consciousness he began a sprightly conversation <\s>

<s> before the end of the day's amusements many more gentlemen of lady clavering's acquaintance came up to her carriage and chatted with the party which it contained <\s>
<s> the worthy lady was in high spirits and good humour laughing and talking according to her wont and offering refreshments to all her friends until her ample baskets and bottles were emptied and her servants and postillions were in such a royal state of excitement as servants and postillions commonly are upon the derby day <\s>
<s> the major remarked that some of the visitors to the carriage appeared to look with rather queer and meaning glances towards its owner <\s>
<s> how easily she takes it <\s>

<s> has anybody lost any money <\s>

<s> the carriage wheeled off the course and took its way londonwards not the least brilliant equipage in that vast and picturesque procession <\s>
<s> the tipsy drivers dashed gallantly over the turf amidst the admiration of foot passengers the ironical cheers of the little donkey carriages and spring vans and the loud objurgations of horse and chaise men with whom the reckless post boys came in contact <\s>
<s> the jolly begum looked the picture of good humour as she reclined on her splendid cushions the lovely sylphide smiled with languid elegance <\s>
<s> many an honest holiday maker with his family wadded into a tax cart many a cheap dandy working his way home on his weary hack admired that brilliant turn out and thought no doubt how happy those swells must be <\s>
<s> strong sat on the box still with a lordly voice calling to the post boys and the crowd <\s>
<s> master frank had been put inside of the carriage and was asleep there by the side of the major dozing away the effects of the constant luncheon and champagne of which he had freely partaken <\s>
<s> the major was revolving in his mind meanwhile the news the receipt of which had made him so grave <\s>
<s> if sir francis clavering goes on in this way pendennis the elder thought this little tipsy rascal will be as bankrupt as his father and grandfather before him <\s>
<s> the begum's fortune can't stand such drains upon it no fortune can stand them she has paid his debts half a dozen times already <\s>
<s> a few years more of the turf and a few coups like this will ruin her <\s>

<s> yes we must have them there again <\s>
<s> there were races there in the old times the good old times <\s>

<s> capital fun said mamma <\s>
